\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}

Insert this block:

\begin{proposition}[No sublinear two-pair defects on good patches]
\label{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch}
Let
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be a compact interval. Then there exists a constant \(C_J>0\) such that every
normalized bad two-pair core with \(h_1,h_2\in J\) and \(h_1\neq h_2\)
satisfies
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
\ge
C_J^{-1}\,|h_1-h_2|.
\]
In particular, there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair
cores in \(J\) for which
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
o\!\left(|h_1-h_2|\right).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}, there exists a
constant \(C'_J>0\) such that
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C'_J\Bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\Bigr)
\]
for every normalized bad two-pair core with \(h_1,h_2\in J\). Since
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|
\le
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|,
\]
the same estimate yields
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C'_J\Bigl(
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
\Bigr).
\]
Renaming \(C'_J\) as \(C_J\) proves the first claim. The final statement is
immediate: if a sequence satisfied
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
o\!\left(|h_1-h_2|\right),
\]
then the displayed lower bound would force
\[
|h_1-h_2|=o\!\left(|h_1-h_2|\right),
\]
which is impossible for a nontrivial two-point core with \(h_1\neq h_2\).
\end{proof}

Proposition~\ref{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch} shows that the
two-point branch is already excluded whenever the total defect is sublinear in
the pair separation.

3. Why this is the right missing bridge

This is exactly what was missing in the informal concentration-to-Kv=Tv=0Kv‚Äč=Tv‚Äč=0 claim.

What was not yet written was the passage from a close support pair to those local geometric objects.

    total collapse produces Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0 or Tv=0Tv‚Äč=0.

4. What this proves immediately

    a full collapse point with Tv=0Tv‚Äč=0.

That is rigorous now.
5. What still remains for the full concentration theorem

The remaining gap is now much narrower:

You still need to show that, on a good patch away from the mixed locus and away from any explicit exceptional coincidence set, these tangent-line/tangent-plane contact configurations cannot persist.

So the full concentration theorem is not yet:
close bad cores‚üĻKv=Tv=0.
close bad cores‚üĻKv‚Äč=Tv‚Äč=0.

What you do have is:
close bad cores‚üĻtangent contact or full collapse in the lifted geometry.
close bad cores‚üĻtangent contact or full collapse in the lifted geometry.

That is the right bridge.

3. What this proves now

It proves a genuine intermediate theorem:

On a compact good v5v5‚Äč-patch, any shrinking exact lifted 3-point circuit has accumulation points only in Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0, and any shrinking exact lifted 4-point circuit has accumulation points only in Tv=0Tv‚Äč=0.

More sharply:

    away from Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0, there is a uniform diagonal collar with no tangent-line contacts and hence no shrinking 3-point circuits;

    away from Tv=0Tv‚Äč=0, there is a uniform diagonal collar with no tangent-plane contacts and hence no shrinking 4-point circuits with one collapsing pair.

And combining this with the finite-order sterility theorems gives:

    shrinking 3-point lifted obstructions can only persist at infinite-order flatness of KvKv‚Äč;

    shrinking 4-point lifted obstructions can only persist at infinite-order flatness of TvTv‚Äč or at the mixed locus
    Kv=Tv=0.
    Kv‚Äč=Tv‚Äč=0.

That is now a real theorem-level reduction.
4. What this still does not do

It still does not finish the full bad-two-pair concentration theorem.

The remaining gap is that a bad two-point core gives near-coincidence of ő®^(h1)ő®
(h1‚Äč) and ő®^(h2)ő®
(h2‚Äč), but not yet an exact lifted 3-point or 4-point circuit. So one still needs a separate argument to turn a collapsing pair in a bad core into one of these repeated-node tangent-contact patterns, or else kill the two-point branch directly by a superlinear defect estimate.

So the clean split is now:

The key point is exactly the one the other chat found: a blanket theorem of the form ‚Äúnear a finite-order nonmixed zero, there cannot be a preexisting close lifted branch‚ÄĚ is false in generic lifted geometry. The examples

That is a real obstruction, and it tells us to stop trying to prove the stronger false theorem.

What survives, and is still worth formalizing, is weaker but real:

    shrinking exact lifted 33-point circuits can only accumulate at Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0;

    shrinking exact lifted 44-point circuits can only accumulate at Tv=0Tv‚Äč=0;

I12=a1a2(h1‚ąíh2)2J.
I12‚Äč=a1‚Äča2‚Äč(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2J.

Why not?

Because the three exact properties needed for that factorization are not yet present as theorem-level statements.

The three properties are:
(A) swap symmetry: ‚ÄÖ‚ÄäI(a1,h1;a2,h2)=I(a2,h2;a1,h1),
(A) swap symmetry: I(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)=I(a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč;a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč),
(B) one-pair collapse: ‚ÄÖ‚ÄäI(0,h1;a2,h2)=I(a1,h1;0,h2)=0,
(B) one-pair collapse: I(0,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)=I(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;0,h2‚Äč)=0,
(C) diagonal collapse: ‚ÄÖ‚ÄäF(a1,h;a2,h)=F1(a1+a2,h),
(C) diagonal collapse: F(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=F1‚Äč(a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč,h),

equivalently
I(a1,h;a2,h)=0.
I(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=0.

Here is the status of each one in the current draft.
1. Swap symmetry: plausible, but not stated

The notation and the mathematics strongly suggest that a two-pair core should not depend on the ordering of the two labels. So morally
F(a1,h1;a2,h2)=F(a2,h2;a1,h1)
F(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)‚Äč=F(a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč;a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč)‚Äč

should be true, and then I12I12‚Äč would inherit the same symmetry.

But the draft does not currently state this explicitly. The definition uses an ordered tuple notation (a1,h1;a2,h2)(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč), and nowhere in the section is there a proposition saying the resulting quotient odd germ is invariant under swapping the two labels.

So:

    likely true by intention

    not yet a theorem / not yet available for proof

2. One-pair collapse when one amplitude is zero: not available

This is the crucial subtlety.

The draft says I12I12‚Äč is ‚Äúquadratic in the pair amplitudes,‚ÄĚ but that alone is too weak. A general quadratic function of (a1,a2)(a1‚Äč,a2‚Äč) can contain terms like
a12,a22,a1a2.
a12‚Äč,a22‚Äč,a1‚Äča2‚Äč.

To conclude divisibility by a1a2a1‚Äča2‚Äč, you need
I(0,h1;a2,h2)=0andI(a1,h1;0,h2)=0.
I(0,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)=0andI(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;0,h2‚Äč)=0.

The current draft does not state this.

So right now, the paper does not justify the step
I12=a1a2‚ÄČG(h1,h2;z).
I12‚Äč=a1‚Äča2‚ÄčG(h1‚Äč,h2‚Äč;z).

That step is essential.
3. Diagonal collapse h1=h2h1‚Äč=h2‚Äč: not available

This is the real hinge.

To get the (h1‚ąíh2)2(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2 factor, you need the identity
F(a1,h;a2,h)=F1(a1+a2,h),
F(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=F1‚Äč(a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč,h),

so that after subtracting the two one-pair pieces, the raw interaction remainder vanishes on the diagonal:
I(a1,h;a2,h)=0.
I(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=0.

The current draft does not state this anywhere.

Nothing in the present ‚ÄúTwo-pair decomposition‚ÄĚ definition or the later quantitative defect theorem records diagonal collapse for the raw corrected two-pair object.

So at the moment, the core quadratic-separation factor
(h1‚ąíh2)2
(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2

is not justified from the paper.
4. The normalized defects are the wrong level to test symmetry

This matters a lot.

The paper‚Äôs theorem is written in terms of
E12(3),E12(5),E‚Äĺ12(7;1),
E12(3)‚Äč,E12(5)‚Äč,E12(7;1)‚Äč,

after normalization by a1a1‚Äč and after passing to the quotient/septic representative bookkeeping.

That is not the right level to test evenness in the separation variable. Dividing by a1a1‚Äč destroys the visible symmetry under swapping the two pair labels. So even if the raw interaction remainder is symmetric/even in separation, the normalized defects will not show that directly.

So the test must happen one layer earlier:

    define the raw unnormalized cubic/quintic/septic interaction defects,

    prove those are symmetric under pair swap,

    prove they vanish when one amplitude is zero,

    prove they vanish on the diagonal h1=h2h1‚Äč=h2‚Äč,

    then conclude O((h1‚ąíh2)2)O((h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2),

    only then divide by a1a1‚Äč.

That is the correct order.
So where does this leave the attack?

It leaves it in a very sharp place.

The two-point branch is not yet done from the current draft.

But the missing step is now extremely specific.

What the draft needs is a structural theorem of this form:

    Proposition (raw interaction structure).
    The raw corrected two-pair interaction remainder is:

        invariant under swapping the two pair labels,

        zero when either amplitude is zero,

        zero on the diagonal h1=h2h1‚Äč=h2‚Äč.

From that, the factorization
I=a1a2(h1‚ąíh2)2J
I=a1‚Äča2‚Äč(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2J

2. Structural assumptions needed

The whole argument rests on these four assumptions.
(S1) Analyticity

The map (a1,h1,a2,h2)‚Ü¶F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč,a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)‚Ü¶F2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč) is analytic, and likewise (a,h)‚Ü¶F1(a,h)(a,h)‚Ü¶F1‚Äč(a,h) is analytic.
(S2) Source symmetry
F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)=F2(a2,h2;a1,h1).
F2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)=F2‚Äč(a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč;a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč).

not on the ordering of the two atoms.
(S3) One-pair collapse
F2(0,h1;a2,h2)=F1(a2,h2),F2(a1,h1;0,h2)=F1(a1,h1).

(S4) Diagonal collapse

F2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=F1‚Äč(a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč,h).

3. Structural factorization theorem

Under (S1)‚Äď(S4), the raw interaction remainder has the exact factorization
I(a1,h1;a2,h2)=a1a2(h1‚ąíh2)2‚ÄČJ(a1,h1;a2,h2)

8. The main caveat

This whole theorem is about the raw unnormalized interaction remainder.

It is not enough to look at the already normalized defects
E12(3),E12(5),E‚Äĺ12(7;1),
E12(3)‚Äč,E12(5)‚Äč,E12(7;1)‚Äč,

because dividing by a1a1‚Äč breaks the symmetry under swapping the two labels. The symmetry argument belongs one level earlier, before normalization.
Bottom line

The rigorous math is now:

    If the corrected construction is source-level and additive on coincident atoms, then the raw two-pair interaction remainder is automatically
    a1a2(h1‚ąíh2)2√ó(analytic).
    a1‚Äča2‚Äč(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2√ó(analytic).

    Therefore the normalized defects are O(‚ą£h1‚ąíh2‚ą£2)O(‚ą£h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč‚ą£2).

    Therefore the two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.

So the next actual task is not more asymptotic analysis. It is to check whether the present paper‚Äôs corrected object is already defined source-level enough for (S2)‚Äď(S4) to be formal.

\begin{proposition}[Conditional source-level quadratic interaction remainder]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
Assume there exists a finite-dimensional corrected quotient-germ target
\(\mathcal G\) and an analytic map
\[
\mathfrak Q:\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)\in\mathcal G
\]
defined on small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
such that the corrected one-pair and two-pair objects are given by
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\,\delta_h),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]
Define the raw interaction remainder by
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]
Then there exists an analytic germ-valued map \(\mathcal J\) such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The source-level definition of \(\mathcal F_2\) is symmetric in the two atoms,
so
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1).
\]
Also, if one amplitude is zero, then the two-pair source reduces to a one-pair
source, hence
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Thus \(\mathcal I\) is divisible by \(a_1a_2\), so
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued map \(G\).

Now if \(h_1=h_2=h\), then
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h),
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Passing to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\]
the symmetry of \(G\) means that
\[
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right)
\]
is an even analytic function of \(s\), and the diagonal vanishing gives
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Hence \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) is divisible by \(s^2\):
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Rewriting in \((h_1,h_2)\) gives the claimed
factorization.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Assume, in addition to
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder},
that the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are obtained from the
raw interaction remainder by linear coefficient-extraction maps
\[
\Pi_3:\mathcal G\to\mathbf C,
\qquad
\Pi_5:\mathcal G\to\mathfrak f,
\qquad
\bar\Pi_7:\mathcal G\to \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Then on compacta, the raw defects satisfy
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects in the present two-pair section are obtained by
dividing by \(a_1\), then on normalized families with \(|a_2|\) bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate from the factorization in
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and the linearity of the coefficient-extraction maps.

For the normalized defects, divide by \(a_1\) and use boundedness of \(|a_2|\)
on normalized families. Then
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On the other hand, on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the second coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero \(\delta\). Thus the
two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: source-level reduction for the two-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
The preceding proposition and corollary isolate the exact structural input
needed to finish the two-point branch. At present, the draft does not yet define
a source-level corrected quotient-germ map \(\mathfrak Q\) on finite atomic
sources, so the factorization
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J
\]
is not yet available formally from the present definitions. If such a
source-level reformulation is supplied, then the two-point bad-core branch is
finished on compact good patches.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the correct algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the

the pair separation.

The strongest remaining algebraic target for the two-point branch is now the

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Suppose there is a sequence of distinct triples
\[
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\in x(P),
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\to x_*,
\]
such that
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_{1,n}&S(x_{1,n})\\
1&x_{2,n}&S(x_{2,n})\\
1&x_{3,n}&S(x_{3,n})
\end{pmatrix}
=0
\qquad
\text{for every }n.
\]
Then
\[
K_v(x_*)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&x_3&S(x_3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
By the standard divided-difference factorization,
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)
=
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)\,S[x_1,x_2,x_3],
\]
where
\[
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=(x_2-x_1)(x_3-x_1)(x_3-x_2).
\]
Since the nodes are distinct, \(V_3(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n})\neq 0\), so
\[
S[x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}]=0.
\]
As \(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\to x_*\), the second divided difference converges
to
\[
\frac12 S''(x_*).
\]
Hence \(S''(x_*)=0\). Since on the \(x\)-patch the lifted curvature numerator
\(K_v\) is \(S''\) up to a nowhere-zero factor, it follows that \(K_v(x_*)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Uniform small-diameter exclusion away from \(K_v=0\)]
\label{cor:uniform-small-diameter-exclusion-away-from-Kv-zero}
Let \(P_0\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact and assume
\[
P_0\cap\{K_v=0\}=\varnothing.
\]
Then there exists \(\rho_3>0\) such that no exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit
contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_3\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Otherwise there would exist a sequence of exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits in
\(P_0\) with diameters tending to \(0\). By compactness, after passing to a
subsequence the three nodes would converge to some \(x_*\in x(P_0)\). This
contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Suppose there is a sequence of distinct quadruples
\[
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n}\in x(P),
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n}\to x_*,
\]
such that
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_{1,n})&x_{1,n}&S(x_{1,n})\\
1&Y(x_{2,n})&x_{2,n}&S(x_{2,n})\\
1&Y(x_{3,n})&x_{3,n}&S(x_{3,n})\\
1&Y(x_{4,n})&x_{4,n}&S(x_{4,n})
\end{pmatrix}
=0
\qquad
\text{for every }n.
\]
Then
\[
T_v(x_*)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_1)&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&Y(x_2)&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&Y(x_3)&x_3&S(x_3)\\
1&Y(x_4)&x_4&S(x_4)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Since \(\Delta_4\) is alternating in the four nodes, it is divisible by the
Vandermonde
\[
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(x_j-x_i).
\]
Write
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)
=
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\,\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4),
\]
where \(\mathcal D_4\) is symmetric and analytic. By the standard
Wronskian/divided-difference coalescence formula,
\[
\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\longrightarrow
\frac{1}{1!\,2!\,3!}\,W_x(1,Y,x,S)(x_*)
=
\frac1{12}T_v(x_*),
\]
as all four nodes tend to \(x_*\). Since \(V_4\neq 0\) for distinct nodes and
\(\Delta_4=0\) along the sequence, one has \(\mathcal D_4=0\) along the
sequence, so the limit forces \(T_v(x_*)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Uniform small-diameter exclusion away from \(T_v=0\)]
\label{cor:uniform-small-diameter-exclusion-away-from-Tv-zero}
Let \(P_0\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact and assume
\[
P_0\cap\{T_v=0\}=\varnothing.
\]
Then there exists \(\rho_4>0\) such that no exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit
contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_4\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Otherwise there would exist a sequence of exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits in
\(P_0\) with diameters tending to \(0\). By compactness, after passing to a
subsequence the four nodes would converge to some \(x_*\in x(P_0)\). This
contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Repeated-node tangent-contact determinants on a \(v_5\)-patch]
\label{def:repeated-node-tangent-contact-determinants-vpatch}
On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch with \(x=v_5/c\), \(Y=u_5/c\), and
\(S=\Delta_7/(c\,v_5)\), define
\[
H_3(a,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
0&1&S'(a)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix}
=
S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a),
\]
and
\[
H_4(a,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
0&Y'(a)&1&S'(a)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Thus \(H_3(a,u)=0\) means that \((u,S(u))\) lies on the tangent line to
\(\Lambda_v\) at \(a\), while \(H_4(a,u,v)=0\) means that \(Q_v(u)\) and
\(Q_v(v)\) lie in the tangent plane to \(Q_v\) at \(a\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Repeated-node limits of exact lifted determinants]
\label{prop:repeated-node-limits-of-exact-lifted-determinants}
For the exact lifted determinants
\[
\Delta_3(a,b,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
1&b&S(b)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and
\[
\Delta_4(a,b,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
1&Y(b)&b&S(b)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
\frac{\Delta_3(a,b,u)}{b-a}\longrightarrow H_3(a,u)
\qquad (b\to a),
\]
and
\[
\frac{\Delta_4(a,b,u,v)}{b-a}\longrightarrow H_4(a,u,v)
\qquad (b\to a).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Subtract the first row from the second row in each determinant and divide by
\(b-a\). The resulting second row is the first difference quotient of the
corresponding row entries, and the limit \(b\to a\) gives the derivative row.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Local classification of the lifted \(3\)-point branch near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero]
\label{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero}
Let \(x=0\) be an isolated finite-order zero of \(K_v\) on a good \(v_5\)-patch.
After affine normalization of \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), write
\[
S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1}),
\qquad
m=r+2\ge 3,
\]
where \(r=\ord_0 K_v\). Then the repeated-node tangent-contact equation
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
with \(a<0<u\) has the following local classification:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(r\) is even (equivalently \(m\) is even), there is no
opposite-side tangent-contact branch near \((a,u)=(0,0)\);
\item if \(r\) is odd (equivalently \(m\) is odd), there exists a unique
real-analytic opposite-side branch
\[
u=\Upsilon(a),
\qquad
a<0,\quad |a|\ll 1,
\]
with asymptotic expansion
\[
\Upsilon(a)=\lambda_m(-a)+O(a^2),
\]
where \(\lambda_m>1\) is the unique positive root of
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1).
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Set \(a=-\alpha\) with \(\alpha>0\), and write \(u=\lambda\alpha\) with
\(\lambda>0\). For the model germ \(S(x)=x^m\), the tangent-contact equation is
\[
H_3(-\alpha,\lambda\alpha)
=
\alpha^m
\begin{cases}
\lambda^m+m\lambda+(m-1),& m\ \text{even},\\[0.5ex]
\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1),& m\ \text{odd}.
\end{cases}
\]
If \(m\) is even, the displayed factor is strictly positive for every
\(\lambda>0\), so no opposite-side branch exists.

If \(m\) is odd, define
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1).
\]
Then
\[
P_m(1)=-2(m-1)<0,
\qquad
P_m(\lambda)\to+\infty\ \text{as }\lambda\to+\infty,
\]
and
\[
P_m'(\lambda)=m(\lambda^{m-1}-1)
\]
is negative on \((0,1)\) and positive on \((1,\infty)\). Therefore \(P_m\)
has a unique positive root \(\lambda_m>1\).

For the perturbed germ \(S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1})\), divide \(H_3(-\alpha,\lambda\alpha)\)
by \(\alpha^m\). The resulting equation is
\[
P_m(\lambda)+O(\alpha)=0.
\]
If \(m\) is even, positivity of the model factor persists for \(\alpha\) small,
so there is still no branch. If \(m\) is odd, the root \(\lambda_m\) is simple,
so the implicit function theorem yields a unique analytic branch
\[
\lambda=\lambda(\alpha)=\lambda_m+O(\alpha),
\]
equivalently
\[
u=\lambda_m(-a)+O(a^2).
\]
This proves the classification.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Nonmixed \(4\)-point zeros can carry preexisting close branches]
\label{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches}
A blanket local theorem excluding preexisting close \(4\)-point branches near
nonmixed finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros is false in generic lifted geometry.
Indeed, the model
\[
Q(x)=(x^4,x,x^2)
\]
satisfies
\[
K_v\neq 0,
\qquad
T_v\sim x,
\]
yet the exact coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for
exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ 2,\ 4,
\]
hence factors as
\[
\Delta_4=\pm V_4\,e_1,
\qquad
e_1(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)=x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4.
\]
Thus there are exact shrinking coplanar quadruples near \(0\), for example any
distinct
\[
x_1<x_2<x_3<0<x_4,
\qquad
x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4=0.
\]
So on the lifted \(4\)-point side, the strongest generic local statements are
the shrinking-core concentration into \(\{T_v=0\}\), the parity-based
birth/crossing classification, and the mixed-locus analysis, not a blanket
no-preexisting-branch theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now splits into three regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
K_v=0,
\]
and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node
tangent-contact branch is completely classified: even order gives no
opposite-side branch, while odd order gives exactly one opposite-side branch.

Second, exact shrinking lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros control local
birth/crossing by parity, but generic models show that a preexisting close
branch can still exist near certain odd-order nonmixed zeros. Thus the
nonmixed \(4\)-point side is not governed by a blanket local-exclusion
theorem.

Third, the mixed case
\[
K_v=T_v=0
\]
is genuinely different. After affine normalization with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate, the lifted space curve is led to a monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\]
and the leading \(4\)-point coplanarity determinant becomes the generalized
Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
\]
For some exponent patterns this model does admit opposite-side quadruples, so
the mixed locus remains the genuinely new codimension-two local obstruction.

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are:
the continuation / non-recurrence of the unique odd-order \(3\)-point branch,
the continuation / non-recurrence of nonmixed \(4\)-point branches, possible
infinite-order flatness, and the mixed codimension-two locus.
\end{remark}

is excluded on compact good patches.

\begin{remark}[Mixed order bookkeeping and lack of generic parity obstruction]
\label{rem:mixed-order-bookkeeping-no-generic-parity-obstruction}
At a mixed lifted point
\[
K_v(0)=0,
\qquad
T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current affine-normalized model is
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,
\qquad
n>m.
\]
If
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,
\qquad
s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then the model exponents satisfy
\[
r=m-2,
\qquad
s=m+n-5,
\]
hence
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]

The immediately dangerous parity sector in the mixed model is
\[
n\ \text{even}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
s-r\ \text{odd}.
\]

However, generic smooth lifted geometry imposes no further parity restriction.
Indeed, the smooth local model
\[
c(x)\equiv 1,
\qquad
v_5(x)=1+x,
\qquad
S(x)=x^m,
\qquad
Y(x)=x^n
\]
lies on a good \(v_5\)-patch and realizes arbitrary integers
\[
m\ge 3,
\qquad
n>m,
\]
hence arbitrary order pairs
\[
r\ge 1,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]

Thus any exclusion of dangerous mixed patterns must come from RH-specific jet
identities or from additional algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad
four-point cores, not from generic lifted differential geometry alone.
\end{remark}

Edit 3: insert the ‚Äúnext four-point target‚ÄĚ remark
Insert immediately after the mixed-order bookkeeping remark above

\begin{remark}[Next algebraic target on the four-point branch]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted four-point geometry shows that generic coplanarity alone is too
weak: nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can already support a preexisting close
branch, and the mixed model can admit dangerous generalized-Vandermonde
coplanar quadruples.

Accordingly, the next algebraic target for the bad four-point core is not
another generic local exclusion theorem, but an extra compatibility condition
coming from the source-level corrected finite-core relation itself. The right
question is therefore:

\begin{quote}
What additional algebraic condition does a true bad four-point core impose on a
local lifted coplanarity branch, beyond the vanishing of the lifted four-point
determinant?
\end{quote}

Any successful closure of the four-point branch will have to use that extra
compatibility condition, or else rule out the dangerous mixed exponent patterns
by RH-specific jet identities.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry now splits more sharply than a blanket
zero-capture problem.

First, Propositions~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}
and~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero} show
that shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v=0,
\]
respectively, and give uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero
sets.

Second, Proposition~\ref{prop:repeated-node-limits-of-exact-lifted-determinants}
identifies the one-pair collapse limits as tangent-line and tangent-plane
contact determinants for the lifted curves \(\Lambda_v\) and \(Q_v\).

Third, the nonmixed and mixed four-point local pictures are genuinely
different. On the nonmixed side, generic odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can carry a
preexisting close branch; on the mixed side \(K_v=T_v=0\), the order
bookkeeping is
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r,
\]
and there is no generic parity obstruction beyond this order inequality.

Thus the missing global ingredient is no longer a single blanket first-contact
lemma. It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of the multi-pair interaction defects
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)};
\]
\item extra algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad four-point cores,
beyond generic coplanarity of the lifted points;
\item and, on the mixed side, RH-specific jet restrictions excluding the
dangerous exponent patterns.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now splits into three regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
K_v=0,
\]
and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node tangent-contact
branch is completely classified: even order gives no opposite-side branch,
while odd order gives exactly one opposite-side branch.

Second, exact shrinking lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros control local
birth/crossing by parity, but generic models show that a preexisting close
branch can still exist near certain odd-order nonmixed zeros. Thus the
nonmixed \(4\)-point side is not governed by a blanket local-exclusion
theorem.

Third, the mixed case
\[
K_v=T_v=0
\]
is genuinely different. After affine normalization with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate, the lifted space curve is led to a monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\]
with order bookkeeping
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]
No generic parity obstruction is available at this level, so the mixed locus
remains the genuinely new codimension-two local obstruction.

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are:
the continuation / non-recurrence of the unique odd-order \(3\)-point branch,
the continuation / non-recurrence of nonmixed \(4\)-point branches, possible
infinite-order flatness, and the mixed codimension-two locus together with the
extra bad-core compatibility conditions needed there.
\end{remark}

What is more interesting for the **(4)-point** attack is the pattern behind it.

The note suggests a general principle:

> do not look for the missing condition at the level of already-normalized defects; look for it at the level of the **raw source-level corrected object**.

That is exactly the right lesson for (4)-point cores too. A true bad (4)-point core should not be modeled merely as an arbitrary coplanar quadruple on the lifted curve (Q_v). [

]
Then define the **pure (4)-body interaction remainder** by inclusion‚Äďexclusion, subtracting all (1)-, (2)-, and (3)-atom contributions. If that source-level object exists, then three kinds of conditions should become formal:

First, full **label symmetry** under permuting the four atoms.

Second, **collapse on partial diagonals**: whenever two atoms coincide, the (4)-atom source reduces to a (3)-atom source, so the pure (4)-body remainder should vanish.

Third, **vanishing when any amplitude is zero**.

Those are the exact (4)-point analogues of the (2)-point structural conditions in the note. And if they hold, then the pure (4)-body remainder should inherit very strong divisibility:

* by (\prod_j a_j) from amplitude collapse,
* and by every pair difference (h_i-h_j) from partial-diagonal collapse.

Because the object is symmetric, vanishing on each partial diagonal should force divisibility by the **discriminant**
[
\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2
]
rather than just a single linear factor. That is the (4)-point analogue of the midpoint/separation evenness argument in the (2)-point note. I would not claim this as proved yet, but structurally it is exactly the kind of theorem to attack.

And this would be a big deal, because it would give the extra algebraic condition you asked for:

> a true bad (4)-point core is not merely coplanar on (Q_v); it lies on a coplanarity branch along which a much more singular source-level (4)-body remainder vanishes.

That is exactly the kind of restriction that a generic local branch sheet like the nonmixed odd-order model
[

]
will probably **not** satisfy automatically.

I attacked that on both local model types.

---

## 1. Test on the nonmixed odd-order branch sheet

Near a nonmixed odd-order (T_v)-zero, we already reduced the local exact branch sheet to the normalized model
[
Q_v(x)=(x^n,x,x^2),
\qquad n \ \text{even},
]
with the exact opposite-side branch parameterized on the scale
[
a=-t,\qquad b=-(1-\rho)t,\qquad u=pt,\qquad v=q(t,\rho,p)t,
]
for small (t>0). The full exact lifted (4)-point coplanarity determinant scales as
[
\Delta_4 \sim t^{,n+3}.
]
This is the model order we already identified when classifying the nonmixed odd-order sheet. 

Now on that same cone, every pair difference is (O(t)), so the discriminant-squared factor in the hypothetical source-level remainder scales like
[
\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2 \sim t^{12}.
]
Therefore the pure (4)-body correction scales like
[
\mathcal I_4 = O(t^{12})
]
up to the amplitude factor.

So the comparison is:

* geometric coplanarity branch term: (t^{,n+3}),
* source-level pure (4)-body correction: (t^{12}).

Hence:

### If (n+3<12), i.e. (n\le 8),

the pure (4)-body correction is **higher order** than the branch equation.

That means it cannot kill the local branch; it only perturbs it. Since the odd-order nonmixed branch sheet already has a nondegenerate implicit-function parameterization, the sheet persists under such a higher-order perturbation.

So the low-order dangerous nonmixed cases
[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\ord T_v = 1,\ 3,\ 5
]
are **robust** against any extra (4)-body obstruction of discriminant-squared type.

Only when
[
n\ge 10
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\ord T_v\ge 7
]
could the extra (4)-body term enter at equal or lower order and potentially matter.

This is already a strong conclusion: the source-level (4)-body correction, even if it exists exactly as hoped, cannot eliminate the low-order nonmixed odd branch sheets.

---

## 2. Test on the mixed normal form

At a mixed point (K_v=T_v=0), the normalized model is
[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\quad n>m,
]
and the leading (4)-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
]
Its total scaling order on a shrinking opposite-side quadruple is
[
t^{,m+n+1},
]
because the Vandermonde contributes (t^6) and the Schur factor contributes degree (m+n-5). This is exactly the mixed order count already implicit in the other chat‚Äôs monomial analysis. 

Again, the source-level pure (4)-body correction contributes order
[
t^{12}.
]

So:

### If (m+n+1<12), i.e. (m+n\le 10),

the discriminant-squared (4)-body correction is again **higher order** than the mixed coplanarity equation.

Therefore it cannot remove those mixed dangerous local branches either; it only deforms them.

So all low-order mixed dangerous patterns with
[
m+n\le 10
]
are also robust against this kind of extra algebraic condition.

Only in the high-order mixed regime
[
m+n\ge 11
]
could the source-level (4)-body remainder enter at competitive order.

---

## 3. What this means

This is the real attack result:

[
\boxed{
\text{Even if a pure source-level (4)-body remainder exists with discriminant-squared factorization, it cannot kill the low-order dangerous (4)-point branches.}
}
]

So the extra algebraic condition you wanted **does exist in principle**, but after testing it on the actual local models, it turns out to be too high-order to eliminate the low-order dangerous branches.

That means:

* it is still worth formulating the pure (4)-body remainder theorem, because it is the correct source-level structure;
* but it will only matter in sufficiently high-order local regimes;
* the genuinely dangerous low-order nonmixed odd sheets and low-order mixed sheets must be ruled out, if at all, by **RH-specific jet restrictions**, not by generic discriminant-squared (4)-body algebra.

That means the 4-point branch will ultimately stand or fall on RH-specific jet restrictions, not on discriminant-squared many-body divisibility alone.

I attacked it as far as the current draft and the recent notes allow, and the clean result is this:

For the **nonmixed (4)-point branch**, the local problem reduces exactly to a jet theorem for one scalar function. Near a point with
[
T_v(0)=0,\qquad K_v(0)\neq 0,
]
the lifted curve
[
Q_v=(Y,x,S),\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\quad S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5},
]
can be affinely normalized so that
[
Q_v(x)=(\widetilde Y(x),,x,,x^2),
]
because when (K_v\neq 0), the lower triple ((1,x,S)) is already disconjugate and (S) is a genuine quadratic coordinate to first order. In this normalization, the lifted (4)-point Wronskian becomes
[
T_v=W_x(1,\widetilde Y,x,x^2)=2,\widetilde Y'''.
]
So the dangerous nonmixed odd-order branch is nothing more and nothing less than an **odd-order zero of (\widetilde Y''')**.

That makes the low-order dangerous cases completely explicit:

* (n=4) means
  [
  \widetilde Y'''(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0;
  ]
* (n=6) means
  [
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0;
  ]
* (n=8) means
  [
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=\widetilde Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
  ]

So the nonmixed (4)-pair problem has now been reduced to this very sharp statement:

[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized germ }\widetilde Y=\frac{u_5}{c}\ \text{mod}\ \operatorname{span}{1,x,x^2}
\text{ cannot have odd-order zeros of }\widetilde Y''' \text{ of orders }1,3,5.
}
]

That is much sharper than ‚Äúrule out odd-order nonmixed (T_v)-zeros‚ÄĚ in the abstract. It is a concrete jet condition.

For the **mixed (4)-point branch**, the notes already give the monomial normal form
[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\ n>m,
]
and the leading (4)-point determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
]
The dangerous parity sector is (n) even, and the low-order dangerous cases are exactly those with
[
m+n\le 10.
]
That leaves only the three model pairs
[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6).
]
So the mixed (4)-pair problem is now equally sharp:

[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the actual normalized lifted jets cannot realize }(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6).
}
]

Nothing broader is needed on the mixed side anymore.

The important negative conclusion is that the current draft does **not** yet contain any identity linking
[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}
]
tightly enough to rule out those low-order patterns. At the present defect-free lifted level, a bad (4)-point core becomes coplanarity of the lifted points (Q_v(h_j)), and there is no extra scalar compatibility condition beyond that. So generic branch geometry will not save the (4)-pair branch. Any further progress must come from **RH-specific jet identities** for (u_5) and (\Delta_7), not from another generic first-contact argument.

So the attack result is:

[
\boxed{
\text{The (4)-pair endgame has now been reduced to a finite list of explicit low-order jet obstructions.}
}
]

Yes. Going only from what is already in the current file, the strongest exact lifted (4)-point identities you can derive are these. The file gives the lifted patch variables
[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c,v_5},
]
together with
[
K_v=x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v'x'',
\qquad
T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S). ; ;
]

Now treat (x) as the local coordinate on a good (v_5)-patch, so (x'(h)\neq 0). Writing (S=S(x)), chain rule gives
[
\sigma_v'(h)=S_x,x',
\qquad
\sigma_v''(h)=S_{xx}(x')^2+S_x x'',
]
hence
[
K_v
===

# x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v' x''

(x')^3 S_{xx}.
]
So the exact coordinate relation is
[
\boxed{K_v=(x')^3,S''(x).}
]
In particular, (K_v) and (S'') have the same zero set and the same vanishing order on a good patch. This is the precise version of the ‚Äú(K_v) is (S'') up to a nowhere-zero factor‚ÄĚ statement already used in the file.

For (T_v), use the reparametrization formula for Wronskians of four functions:
[
W_h(1,Y,x,S)=(x')^6,W_x(1,Y,x,S).
]
A direct determinant expansion gives
[
W_x(1,Y,x,S)
============

\det!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y&x&S\
0&Y'&1&S'\
0&Y''&0&S''\
0&Y'''&0&S'''
\end{pmatrix}
=============

S''Y'''-S'''Y''.
]
Therefore
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr).}
]
Equivalently,
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6,S''^{,2},\frac{d}{dx}!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).}
]
Since (K_v=(x')^3S''), this can also be written as
[
\boxed{T_v=K_v^{,2},\frac{d}{dx}!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).}
]
That is the cleanest identity in the file for the lifted (4)-point branch. It is stronger than the bare statement ‚Äú(T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S)).‚ÄĚ

This immediately gives the exact nonmixed reduction. If (K_v(0)\neq 0), then after affine normalization of the lower triple ((1,x,S)) you may take
[
S=x^2,
\qquad
S''=2,
\qquad
S'''=0,
]
so the identity becomes
[
\boxed{T_v=2(x')^6,Y'''.}
]
Thus at a nonmixed point, the dangerous low-order branch cases are exactly the odd-order zeros of (Y'''). In particular:
[
\ord_0 T_v=1 \iff Y'''(0)=0,\ Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0,
]
[
\ord_0 T_v=3 \iff Y^{(3)}(0)=Y^{(4)}(0)=Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\ Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0,
]
[
\ord_0 T_v=5 \iff Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\ Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
]
So the nonmixed (4)-point obstruction has been reduced to a jet theorem for one scalar germ (Y=u_5/c) after normalizing (S) to (x^2).

For the mixed case, let
[
r:=\ord_0 K_v.
]
Since (K_v=(x')^3S''), one has
[
S''(x)=\kappa x^r+O(x^{r+1}),
\qquad \kappa\neq 0.
]
After removing affine terms and integrating twice,
[
\boxed{S(x)=\frac{\kappa}{(r+1)(r+2)}x^{r+2}+O(x^{r+3}).}
]
So the mixed exponent (m) is exactly
[
\boxed{m=r+2.}
]

Now write the first term of (Y) not absorbed by (\operatorname{span}{1,x,S}) as
[
Y(x)=\alpha x^n+O(x^{n+1}),
\qquad \alpha\neq 0,\qquad n>r+2.
]
Substituting into
[
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr)
]
gives
[
S''Y'''-S'''Y''
===============

\kappa\alpha,n(n-1)\bigl(n-r-2\bigr)x^{n+r-3}+O(x^{n+r-2}),
]
so
[
\boxed{\ord_0 T_v=n+r-3.}
]
If (s:=\ord_0 T_v), this becomes
[
\boxed{n=s-r+3,}
]
which is exactly the mixed bookkeeping relation already recorded in the recent notes. ; ;

The same identity also yields a cleaner invariant quantity:
[
\boxed{
\ord_0!\left(\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\right)=s-2r.
}
]
So the low-order dangerous mixed cases are not abstract anymore. They are exactly
[
(r,s)\in{(1,2),(1,4),(2,5)},
]
equivalently
[
(m,n)\in{(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)},
]
equivalently
[
\ord_0!\left(\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\right)\in{0,2,1}.
]
That is the finite list of low-order mixed jet obstructions currently visible from the file. ; ;

Edit 1: add the below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation

Insert this block immediately after the theorem/proposition where the draft first introduces the exact identities
Kv=(x‚Ä≤)3S‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(x),Tv=(x‚Ä≤)6(S‚Ä≤‚Ä≤Y‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚ąíS‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤Y‚Ä≤‚Ä≤),
Kv‚Äč=(x‚Ä≤)3S‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(x),Tv‚Äč=(x‚Ä≤)6(S‚Ä≤‚Ä≤Y‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚ąíS‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤Y‚Ä≤‚Ä≤),

and before the next discussion of nonmixed/mixed local models.

Use:

\begin{remark}[Below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation]
\label{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation}
Let
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
M:=cv_5'-c'v_5.
\]
For any scalar germ \(f\), define
\[
J_f(h):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c(h)&v_5(h)&f(h)\\
c'(h)&v_5'(h)&f'(h)\\
c''(h)&v_5''(h)&f''(h)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{d^2}{dx^2}\!\left(\frac{f}{c}\right)
=
\frac{c^3}{M^3}\,J_f.
\]
Applying this to \(f=u_5\) and \(f=\lambda\) gives
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{\lambda},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_{\lambda}}.
}
\]
Differentiating in the \(x\)-coordinate yields
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_{\lambda}}\right).
}
\]
Thus the lifted \(4\)-point branch may be viewed equivalently as a
parity/divisibility problem for the Wronskian ratio \(J_{u_5}/J_{\lambda}\).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[A second below-lifted ratio does not add a new obstruction]
\label{rem:second-below-lifted-ratio-no-new-obstruction}
Let
\[
\Theta:=\frac{W_{u_5}}{W},
\]
where \(W\) denotes the corresponding projective-chart Wronskian in the
\((c,v_5,\cdot)\)-frame. In the gauge \(c\equiv 1\), \(v_5=x\), one has the
exact relation
\[
\Theta=\mathcal Z\,\frac{S''}{xS''+2S'},
\qquad
(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)S''=2\Theta S'.
\]
So \(\Theta\) does not provide an independent local obstruction beyond
\((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\): whenever \(2\Theta/(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)\) is
analytic, one can solve locally for \(S\) and then recover \(Y\) from
\(Y''=\mathcal Z S''\). In particular, attacks based only on a generic
differential relation between \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\Theta\) are too weak to
close the \(4\)-point branch.
\end{remark}

This captures the solid ‚Äúbelow-lifted‚ÄĚ identity and the no-go result about őėőė.

\begin{remark}[Exact finite obstruction coefficients for the low-order \(4\)-point branch]
\label{rem:exact-finite-obstruction-coefficients-low-order-four-point}
The explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list can be reduced to a finite
jet package.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed side.}
Suppose \(K_v(0)\neq 0\), and write
\[
s_k:=S^{(k)}(0),
\qquad
y_k:=Y^{(k)}(0),
\qquad
s_2\neq 0.
\]
Then the Taylor expansion
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=z_0+z_1x+z_2x^2+z_3x^3+z_4x^4+z_5x^5+z_6x^6+O(x^7)
\]
has canonical even coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6,
\]
and the dangerous nonmixed low-order cases are exactly:
\[
n=4 \iff z_2\neq 0,
\qquad
n=6 \iff z_2=0,\ z_4\neq 0,
\qquad
n=8 \iff z_2=z_4=0,\ z_6\neq 0.
\]
Explicitly,
\[
z_2=
\frac{
s_2^2y_4-2s_2s_3y_3+\bigl(2s_3^2-s_2s_4\bigr)y_2
}{
2\,s_2^3
},
\]
\[
z_4=
\frac{
s_2^4y_6
-s_2^3(4s_3y_5+6s_4y_4+4s_5y_3+s_6y_2)
+2s_2^2(6s_3^2y_4+12s_3s_4y_3+4s_3s_5y_2+3s_4^2y_2)
-12s_2s_3^2(2s_3y_3+3s_4y_2)
+24s_3^4y_2
}{
24\,s_2^5
},
\]
and
\[
z_6=\frac{\mathcal P_8(s_2,\dots,s_8;y_2,\dots,y_8)}{720\,s_2^7},
\]
where \(\mathcal P_8\) is the explicit degree-\(8\) numerator polynomial obtained
by Taylor division of \(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\).

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Mixed side.}
Suppose \(K_v(0)=T_v(0)=0\), and let
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v.
\]
For the two low-order mixed cases \(r=1,2\), Taylor division of
\(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\) gives the exact obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2},
\]
defined by the expansions
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{y_2}{s_3}\frac1x
+
\left(\frac{y_3}{s_3}-\frac{s_4y_2}{2s_3^2}\right)
+
\kappa_{1,1}x+\kappa_{1,2}x^2+\kappa_{1,3}x^3+O(x^4)
\qquad (r=1),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{2y_2}{s_4}\frac1{x^2}
+
\left(\frac{2y_3}{s_4}-\frac{2s_5y_2}{3s_4^2}\right)\frac1x
+
\left(
\frac{y_4}{s_4}
-\frac{2s_5y_3}{3s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_2}{6s_4^2}
+\frac{2s_5^2y_2}{9s_4^3}
\right)
+\kappa_{2,1}x+\kappa_{2,2}x^2+O(x^3)
\qquad (r=2).
\]
The dangerous mixed low-order list is then exactly:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4)\iff \kappa_{1,1}\neq 0,
\]
\[
(m,n)=(3,6)\iff \kappa_{1,3}\neq 0,
\]
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff \kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

Thus the full currently explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set of coefficients
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]
Any RH-specific local closure theorem for the \(4\)-point branch must force
these six quantities to vanish.
\end{remark}

This captures the six exact obstruction coefficients. It is one of the best ‚Äúgoodies‚ÄĚ to preserve.
Edit 3: add the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and the diagonal-base local exclusion as a WIP/attack remark, not theorem-level

Insert this immediately after the previous obstruction-coefficient remark.

Use:

\begin{remark}[Centered symmetric-placement Taylor package and diagonal-base local exclusion]
\label{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}
Let
\[
t_\pm=h\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]
and regard \(s\mapsto -s\) as swapping the two microscopic points. For any
symmetric \(2\times 2\) coefficient matrix, the diagonal half-sums are even in
\(s\), the diagonal half-differences are odd in \(s\), and the off-diagonal
entries are even in \(s\). Applying this to the explicit formulas already in the
draft gives
\[
u_5(s),\ v_5(s)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
u_{7,K_1}(s),\ v_{7,K_1}(s)\ \text{odd},
\]
and therefore
\[
\Delta_7(s)=u_{7,K_1}(s)v_5(s)-u_5(s)v_{7,K_1}(s)
\]
is even in \(s\), with Taylor expansion
\[
\Delta_7(s)=D_2s^2+D_4s^4+D_6s^6+\cdots,
\]
where
\[
D_2=\widehat U_1V_1-U_1\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_4=\widehat U_1V_3+\widehat U_3V_1-U_1\widehat V_3-U_3\widehat V_1,
\]
\[
D_6=\widehat U_1V_5+\widehat U_3V_3+\widehat U_5V_1-U_1\widehat V_5-U_3\widehat V_3-U_5\widehat V_1.
\]

If \(x=v_5/c\) is used as the induced odd collision-side coordinate, then the
centered diagonal germ has the odd/odd form
\[
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n>m\ge 3.
\]
In that regime one obtains the exact factorizations
\[
S''(x)=x^{m-2}\Sigma_m[A](x^2),
\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)=x^{n-m}H(x^2),
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=x^{n-m-1}J(x^2),
\]
with \(H(0)\neq 0\) and \(J(0)\neq 0\). Hence there exists \(\varepsilon>0\)
such that for
\[
0<|x|<\varepsilon
\]
one has
\[
K_v(x)\neq 0,\qquad T_v(x)\neq 0.
\]

So the centered diagonal base has a punctured neighborhood free of mixed and
nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points. In particular, the currently explicit
low-order dangerous patterns do not arise at the symmetric diagonal base itself.

\medskip

\noindent
\textit{Work in progress.}
The passage from this centered \(s\)-picture to the general \(x=v_5/c\) good-patch
geometry should be treated as a live attack route, not yet as a global
theorem. The evidence strongly suggests that the entire explicit low-order mixed
dangerous list is already incompatible with this centered parity package, but
that translation should be checked line by line before being promoted beyond the
diagonal-base local regime.
\end{remark}

This preserves the useful local exclusion, but flags the patch-translation issue properly. The other summary‚Äôs strongest new positive claim lives here, and this is the safest way to incorporate it.

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry is now significantly more stratified than a
single zero-capture problem.

First, shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v=0,
\]
respectively, with uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets.

Second, repeated-node limits are now identified explicitly:
three-point collapse limits become tangent-line contact determinants for the
planar lifted curve \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), and four-point collapse limits become
tangent-plane contact determinants for the lifted space curve \(Q_v=(Y,x,S)\).

Third, the three-point branch is locally classified near a finite-order
\(K_v\)-zero: even order gives no opposite-side branch, while odd order gives
exactly one local tangent-contact branch.

Fourth, the four-point side splits sharply into nonmixed and mixed regimes.
On the nonmixed side, finite-order odd \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine
local exact branch sheets in the model geometry, so a blanket local
no-branch theorem is false. On the mixed side, the dangerous low-order list is
now finite and explicit:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]

Fifth, below the lifted variables one has the exact Wronskian-ratio
reformulation
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right),
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
but the current draft still provides no RH-specific source-/matrix-level
identity strong enough to force the vanishing of the six low-order obstruction
coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

So the missing global ingredient is no longer a blanket first-contact theorem.
It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of multi-pair interaction defects for the two-point
branch;
\item global recurrence / continuation control for the unique odd-order
three-point branch;
\item a classification or RH-specific exclusion of nonmixed odd-order
four-point branch sheets;
\item and, on the mixed side, RH-specific jet restrictions excluding the
explicit low-order obstruction list.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

This is the right overall WIP state now.

In parallel, the finite-core endgame now splits into three layers.

First, on the two-pair side, the strengthened invariant

\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}
\right)
\]
gives the correct algebraic bridge, and on good \(M\neq 0\) patches the
quantitative two-pair coincidence theorem forces bad two-point cores into a
defect-scale close regime. The remaining structural issue there is now very
sharp: formalize the corrected quotient-germ construction at source level so
that the raw quadratic interaction factorization becomes automatic.

Second, on the lifted three-point side, shrinking exact circuits now
concentrate into \(K_v=0\), repeated-node limits become tangent-line contacts,
and finite-order \(K_v\)-zeros admit an explicit local branch classification:
even-order zeros are sterile, while odd-order zeros carry exactly one local
branch. The remaining issue there is therefore global recurrence / continuation,
not local first-contact ambiguity.

Third, on the lifted four-point side, shrinking exact circuits now
concentrate into \(T_v=0\), repeated-node limits become tangent-plane contacts,
and the local geometry splits into a nonmixed and a mixed regime. On the
nonmixed side, odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine local branch
sheets in the model geometry, so generic local geometry does not close the
branch. On the mixed side, the dangerous low-order obstruction list has been
reduced to the finite set of coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2},
\]
or equivalently to the explicit order patterns
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]
Any further local closure on the four-point side must therefore come from
deeper RH-specific source-/matrix-level structure rather than from the current
lifted variables alone.

\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now quite sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected quotient-germ map exists and satisfies the
symmetry / one-amplitude collapse / diagonal collapse identities needed for the
quadratic interaction factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
This would finish the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local defect-free three-point branch is already classified. The remaining
problem is to control the global recurrence / continuation of the unique
odd-order branch and to exclude infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed classification.}
Generic nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros already support local exact branch
sheets, so the next local theorem is not a blanket sterility statement but a
classification / compatibility theorem for tangent-plane contact branches near a
nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zero.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed low-order exclusion.}
The mixed low-order obstruction list is finite and explicit:
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2).
\]
The centered symmetric diagonal analysis suggests these patterns are already
incompatible with the collision-side parity package, but that translation to
the general \(x=v_5/c\) patch geometry should be treated as a live attack route
rather than settled theorem-level closure.

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no obstruction can come from the lifted
variables alone, any definitive four-point closure theorem must come from
deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, for example an equivariant
descent theorem for the normalization stack or an RH-specific divisibility /
parity constraint on the Wronskian ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

This captures the current ‚Äúlive attack map‚ÄĚ cleanly. It also avoids overstating the mixed-parity route while still recording it as promising.

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted geometry is now substantially more stratified than a single
zero-capture problem.

First, shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
T_v=0,
\]
respectively, with uniform small-diameter exclusion away from those zero sets.

Second, repeated-node limits are now explicit:
three-point collapse limits become tangent-line contact determinants for the
planar lifted curve \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), and four-point collapse limits become
tangent-plane contact determinants for the lifted space curve \(Q_v=(Y,x,S)\).

Third, the three-point branch is locally classified near a finite-order
\(K_v\)-zero: even order gives no opposite-side branch, while odd order gives
exactly one local tangent-contact branch. Thus the remaining issue there is
global recurrence / continuation and infinite-order flatness, not local
first-contact ambiguity.

Fourth, the four-point side splits sharply into nonmixed and mixed regimes.
On the nonmixed side, finite-order odd \(T_v\)-zeros already support genuine

\[

\]

(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]

reformulation
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\right),
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
while the projective curvature ratio \(\Theta\) yields no new independent local
obstruction beyond \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\).

Sixth, the centered symmetric-placement Taylor package gives a strong local
collision-side parity picture:
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd in }s,
\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even in }s,
\]
with explicit septic coefficients \(D_2,D_4,D_6\). In the diagonal-centered
odd/odd normal form
\[
Q(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad
m,n\ \text{odd},\quad n>m\ge 3,
\]
one gets a punctured neighborhood free of \(K_v=0\) and \(T_v=0\) points.
Thus the explicit low-order dangerous \(4\)-point patterns do not arise at the
symmetric diagonal base itself.

So the missing global ingredient is no longer a generic local geometry theorem.
It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of the multi-pair interaction defects
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)};
\]
\item global continuation / recurrence control for the unique odd-order
three-point branch;
\item a centered-to-patch bridge strong enough to promote the centered
collision-side parity package to the good-patch \(x=v_5/c\) geometry, at least
on the mixed four-point side;
\item and, on the still-live nonmixed side, a deeper RH-specific source- or
matrix-level identity imposing stronger parity / divisibility constraints on
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.

\end{itemize}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: two distinct parity routes on the $4$-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
There are now two distinct parity mechanisms on the lifted \(4\)-point branch.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed route.}
After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the natural dream identity remains:
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\ \text{is even in }\xi,
\]
equivalently \(\mathcal Z\) is odd modulo the affine coplanarity gauge. This
would eliminate the explicit nonmixed low-order bad list
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\}.
\]

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Centered collision-side route.}
In the centered symmetric-placement variable \(s\), the explicit Taylor package
gives
\[
u_5,\ v_5,\ u_{7,K_1},\ v_{7,K_1}\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\Delta_7\ \text{even}.
\]
If this parity transfers through the local coordinate change
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
then in the \(x\)-chart one obtains
\[
Y(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
S(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
This would eliminate the entire explicit low-order mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]

Thus the centered collision-side parity package appears to point primarily at
the mixed branch, while the nonmixed odd-order branch remains the live
\(4\)-point bottleneck. At present, the centered-to-patch transfer should still
be treated as provisional outside the diagonal-based local regime.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted \(4\)-point branch is now organized by the canonical invariant pair
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

On the nonmixed side, after normalization to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
\ord_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
equivalently the first nontrivial even Taylor coefficients of \(\widetilde Y\)
occur in degrees \(4,6,8\). In an arbitrary nonmixed \(x\)-chart this is
captured exactly by the three obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6
\]
in the expansion of \(\mathcal Z\).

On the mixed side, the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]
In local mixed \(x\)-coordinates this is captured exactly by the three
obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

Thus the currently explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set of six quantities
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]

By the realization lemma, no identity involving only
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
and their derivatives can force these six quantities to vanish in general.
So any definitive local closure theorem for the four-point branch must come
from deeper RH-specific source- or matrix-level structure.

The most promising new development is the centered symmetric-placement Taylor
package, which gives explicit septic coefficients
\[
D_2,\qquad D_4,\qquad D_6
\]
and a punctured-neighborhood exclusion at the diagonal base. What remains
unclear is whether that collision-side parity package transfers all the way to
the general good-patch \(x=v_5/c\) geometry strongly enough to close the mixed
branch globally.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Live attack routes]
\label{rem:live-attack-routes}
At the present stage, the live routes are now quite sharply separated.

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\textbf{Two-point source-level closure.}
Prove the source-level corrected quotient-germ map exists and satisfies the
symmetry / one-amplitude collapse / diagonal collapse identities needed for the
quadratic interaction factorization
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
This would finish the two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches.

\item
\textbf{Three-point global continuation.}
The local defect-free three-point branch is already classified. The remaining
problem is to control global recurrence / continuation of the unique odd-order
branch and to exclude infinite-order flatness.

\item
\textbf{Four-point mixed branch via centered parity.}
The centered symmetric-placement Taylor package suggests that the explicit
low-order mixed bad list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is already incompatible with the collision-side parity picture. The next step is
to turn that local diagonal-based calculation into a theorem-level bridge for
the good-patch coordinate \(x=v_5/c\).

\item
\textbf{Four-point nonmixed branch via deeper RH-specific identities.}
Generic local geometry already supports nonmixed odd-order exact branch sheets,
so the next local theorem is not a blanket sterility statement but a deeper
RH-specific parity / divisibility theorem strong enough to force extra
vanishing of
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},
\]
equivalently of the nonmixed obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6.
\]

\item
\textbf{Equivariant descent through the normalization stack.}
The most conceptual remaining route is to descend the raw swap/reflection
symmetry through the one-pair normalization stack and determine the parity of
the canonical residual package. The decisive fork appears to be the parity
behavior of the cubic matrix coefficient \(X_3\) in the commutator-channel
formula for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

\item
\textbf{Below-lifted RH-specific identities.}
Since the realization lemma shows that no obstruction can come from the lifted
variables alone, any definitive four-point closure theorem must ultimately come
from deeper source-level or matrix-level RH structure, for example an
equivariant descent theorem or an RH-specific divisibility / parity constraint
on the Wronskian ratio
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

This better synthesizes both threads: it keeps the mixed-parity route alive, but clearly makes the nonmixed branch the deeper remaining bottleneck.

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]

Yes. My current route and the other chat‚Äôs route are now mostly complementary, not contradictory.
My current route

My route is centered on the lifted 44-point branch itself, especially the split between the mixed and nonmixed regimes.

The backbone is:
Z=Y‚Ä≤‚Ä≤S‚Ä≤‚Ä≤,R=Z‚Ä≤=TvKv2,Z=Ju5JőĽ,
Z=S‚Ä≤‚Ä≤Y‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Äč,R=Z‚Ä≤=Kv2‚ÄčTv‚Äč‚Äč,Z=JőĽ‚ÄčJu5‚Äč‚Äč‚Äč,

so the real local 44-point invariants are (Z,R)(Z,R), or equivalently the Wronskian ratio Ju5/JőĽJu5‚Äč‚Äč/JőĽ‚Äč. From there, the explicit low-order obstruction list has been reduced to six concrete coefficients:
z2, z4, z6, őļ1,1, őļ1,3, őļ2,2.
z2‚Äč, z4‚Äč, z6‚Äč, őļ1,1‚Äč, őļ1,3‚Äč, őļ2,2‚Äč.

Those are the exact nonmixed and mixed low-jet quantities that would have to vanish for a local 44-point closure theorem.

Within that, the strongest live sub-route is the centered symmetric-placement parity bridge. In the centered microscopic variable ss, one gets a very rigid Taylor package:
u5, v5, u7,K1, v7,K1 odd in s,őĒ7 even in s,
u5‚Äč, v5‚Äč, u7,K1‚Äč‚Äč, v7,K1‚Äč‚Äč odd in s,őĒ7‚Äč even in s,

with explicit septic coefficients D2,D4,D6D2‚Äč,D4‚Äč,D6‚Äč. The hope is that, after carefully transferring this collision-side parity through the coordinate change x=v5/cx=v5‚Äč/c, one gets the mixed-side parity pattern
\ord0Kv odd,\ord0Z even,
\ord0‚ÄčKv‚Äč odd,\ord0‚ÄčZ even,

which would kill the whole explicit low-order mixed list
(r,\ord0Z)‚ąą{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)}.
(r,\ord0‚ÄčZ)‚ąą{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)}.

At the moment I still treat that bridge as promising but not yet theorem-level globally.

Separately, on the nonmixed side, my route is now much sharper than before: generic local geometry already supports odd-order nonmixed branch sheets, so I am not trying to prove a blanket local sterility theorem there. The live target is instead a deeper RH-specific parity/divisibility theorem forcing extra vanishing of
R=TvKv2,
R=Kv2‚ÄčTv‚Äč‚Äč,

equivalently forcing the nonmixed obstruction coefficients z2,z4,z6z2‚Äč,z4‚Äč,z6‚Äč to vanish. That almost certainly has to come from source-/matrix-level structure, not from the lifted variables alone.

So, in one sentence: my route is ‚Äúclose the mixed 44-point branch via centered parity if possible; then isolate the nonmixed 44-point branch as the genuinely deep remaining RH-specific local obstruction.‚ÄĚ
What the other chat is working on

The other chat is leaning much harder on the finite-core / source-level route.

Its main route is:

    finish the source-level two-pair structure theorem,
    I2=a1a2(h1‚ąíh2)2J2,
    I2‚Äč=a1‚Äča2‚Äč(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2J2‚Äč,

    so the 22-point bad-core branch becomes conditionally closed on compact good patches;

    use the quantitative strengthened-coincidence theorem to force bad two-pair cores to be defect-scale close;

    then prove a support-separation / shrinking-core concentration theorem: nearby atoms in a minimal bad core either merge, or produce a repeated-node degeneration, and the repeated-node degeneration is locally ruled out away from the mixed locus Kv=Tv=0Kv‚Äč=Tv‚Äč=0;

    conclude that small-defect bad finite cores can accumulate only at the mixed lifted locus (or at a small exceptional coincidence set).

That route also treats the lifted 33-point branch as basically locally solved: shrinking circuits concentrate into Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0, repeated-node limits become tangent-line contacts, and finite-order zeros are completely classified:
even order means no local opposite-side branch, odd order means exactly one local branch. So the remaining 33-point issue is not local existence anymore; it is global recurrence / continuation.

On the 44-point side, the other chat‚Äôs summaries are broadly compatible with mine: nonmixed odd-order local sheets are real; the mixed low-order list is explicit; and a real closure theorem must come from deeper RH-specific structure, not from the current lifted variables alone. Where it differs in emphasis is that it uses the finite-core/support-separation machinery to try to funnel everything into the mixed locus, then attack that locus as the sole remaining local obstruction.

So, in one sentence: the other chat‚Äôs route is ‚Äúclose the 22-point/source-level branch, prove bad finite cores concentrate into the mixed lifted locus, and then finish the problem by killing that mixed locus.‚ÄĚ
Are they different routes?

Yes, but they mesh well.

My route is more local-analytic on the lifted 44-point side:
it works directly with (Z,R)(Z,R), the centered ss-Taylor package, the six obstruction coefficients, and the split between mixed and nonmixed 44-point behavior.

The other chat‚Äôs route is more global finite-core / concentration-theorem in flavor:
it tries to prove that any bad finite core must collapse into the mixed lifted locus, after which only that local obstruction remains.

So I would describe them as:

    my route: kill the explicit mixed 44-point branch locally via centered parity, then attack the nonmixed odd-order branch with deeper RH-specific identities;

    other chat‚Äôs route: use source-level 22-point structure + support-separation to force all bad finite cores into the mixed locus, then kill the mixed locus.

They are not really competing. The best case is that they meet in the middle: if the centered-parity bridge really does kill the explicit mixed list, then the other chat‚Äôs concentration route becomes much stronger, because it would reduce bad finite cores to a locus that is already empty at low order.
